  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ee5e97ed-18d4-4c9e-b20f-a50b2fcb2804'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer7096288002180494824">قد يلفت انتباهك اسم الرواية "بداية ونهاية "، ويتركك حائرًا متسائلًا، بداية ماذا؟ ونهاية ماذا؟ وسرعان ما ستتبدد تلك التّساؤلات من خلال سير الأحداث، فتدرك أنّ اسم الرّواية يختصر قصّتنا في كلمتين، ويضعها في إطار مُتقن، رسم كاتبنا من خلاله أحداث قصّته، موضّحا أنّ النّهاية لتلك القصّة ما هي إلّا المصير المحتوم لبدايتنا، فالبداية كانت بالموت والنّهاية مع الموت، وما بينهما ما هو </span>
  <span id="freeText7096288002180494824" style="display:none">قد يلفت انتباهك اسم الرواية "بداية ونهاية "، ويتركك حائرًا متسائلًا، بداية ماذا؟ ونهاية ماذا؟ وسرعان ما ستتبدد تلك التّساؤلات من خلال سير الأحداث، فتدرك أنّ اسم الرّواية يختصر قصّتنا في كلمتين، ويضعها في إطار مُتقن، رسم كاتبنا من خلاله أحداث قصّته، موضّحا أنّ النّهاية لتلك القصّة ما هي إلّا المصير المحتوم لبدايتنا، فالبداية كانت بالموت والنّهاية مع الموت، وما بينهما ما هو إلّا مجموعة من التّفاصيل والأحداث تتناول شخصيّات القصّة و تضحياتها، كيف بدأت كلّ منها؟ وكيف انتهت؟ هذا ما سيعرضه لنا الكاتب بإتقان محكم ونسيج متقن، فقد صال وجال في بحور اللّغة وألوانها، ممّا لن يدع مجالا للشّكّ في نفسك بأنّ ما ينقله هو صورة طبق الأصل لواقع نحياه، وستجد نفسك وقد ارتبطت بأبطاله وألفتهم، حتى بتّ تحيا معهم، فمصابهم مصابنا، وحزنهم حزننا، بكينا كما بكوا، وضحكنا حين ضحكوا.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385264587" href="/book/show/7160.The_Beginning_and_the_End">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129949697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6564530569942967263">A book about death. Perhaps because I'm dealing with a death in the family currently I found this story to be quite poignant. I particularly love Mahfouz's way of telling stories and revealing the characters subtly. I put him on the shelf with authors like Morrison, Marquez, and Cisneros -all very similar story tellers who bring you into a fantasy that almost seems as if you've lived it personally.<br/>The quote towards the end about death being more appealing than hope really resonated with me.</span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/143554154?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marjana Simic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marjana Simic" href="/user/show/4871508-marjana-simic">Marjana Simic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385264587" href="/book/show/7160.The_Beginning_and_the_End">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer143554154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12741155035641281477">"What a torture tyrannical passion is. Who says that it resides in the heart? Is it not more likely that it nestles in the mind? This is the secret of insanity."<br/><br/>After their father's sudden death, the mother and her four children struggle to make ends meet. Each member is encountered with different misfortunes that, in one way or the other, affect the rest of the family. The eldest, Hassan, is an outlaw who willingly gets himself into trouble. The daughter, Nefisa, with ugly features, is betrayed</span>
  <span id="freeText12741155035641281477" style="display:none">"What a torture tyrannical passion is. Who says that it resides in the heart? Is it not more likely that it nestles in the mind? This is the secret of insanity."<br /><br />After their father's sudden death, the mother and her four children struggle to make ends meet. Each member is encountered with different misfortunes that, in one way or the other, affect the rest of the family. The eldest, Hassan, is an outlaw who willingly gets himself into trouble. The daughter, Nefisa, with ugly features, is betrayed and wounded beyond repair. Hussein, the middle brother, is forced to sacrifice his bright future for the sake of his younger brother's and for the sake of family's survival. The youngest, Hassanein, wants all good fortune at once, which makes his life even more miserable. Finally, the mother's pain increases as she witnesses her children's fates.<br /><br />From the beginning I couldn't put this book down. All the family characters are so lovable and each going through unimaginable suffering that both unites them and tears them apart. The one thing they have in common is hope for a better life. However, when a rash decision is made to protect the family's reputation, one is left to wonder was it worth it?<br /><br />"The Beginning and the End" will undoubtedly remain with me for a long time because of the wonderfully written story, larger than life characters, and the theme to which we all can relate to - human suffering. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12741155035641281477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1679383613" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1679383613" />
    <a title="Nick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1927524-nick"><img alt="Nick" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1679383613?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick" href="/user/show/1927524-nick">Nick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385264587" href="/book/show/7160.The_Beginning_and_the_End">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1679383613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13185311834114378699">The great Naguib Mahfouz is one of those rare writers who appeared in the newly post-colonial states of the twentieth century--Pramoedya Toer of Indonesia is another--and whose work, through its intense commitment and breadth of perspective, helps to both develop and define a new nation's literature. Mahfouz' scope was likely wider than perhaps anyone's (although being Egyptian, he had more history to take advantage of, writing several novels about Pharaonic times, and "The Children of Gabelawi"</span>
  <span id="freeText13185311834114378699" style="display:none">The great Naguib Mahfouz is one of those rare writers who appeared in the newly post-colonial states of the twentieth century--Pramoedya Toer of Indonesia is another--and whose work, through its intense commitment and breadth of perspective, helps to both develop and define a new nation's literature. Mahfouz' scope was likely wider than perhaps anyone's (although being Egyptian, he had more history to take advantage of, writing several novels about Pharaonic times, and "The Children of Gabelawi", which addresses the three Abrahamic religions). His range of form was also great, from the dense, unsparing urban novels of Cairo to the brief, almost allegorical "The Thief and the Dogs." "The Beginning and End" finds him squarely in Cairo, his mood angry. A minor functionary dies in the Egypt of the 1930s, leaving his wife and their four children impoverished; the family sells furniture, moves to a dingier apartment, and the daughter even has to solicit work as a dressmaker. Work is not only itself demeaning to such a family, but it forces her to navigate the streets so she can meet with and fit clients in their homes. An elder, ne'er-do-well brother falls in with gangsters. All is sacrificed to the careers of the younger sons who are still in school; money is accepted from the elder brother and the sister but not without disdain for the means by which it is obtained and the snide comments about the dishonor that these occupations threaten to bring onto the family and the younger boys' careers. This is reminiscent of poverty in another city, a continent away: Joyce's Dublin. But Mahfouz' Cairo is without succor; it has no stately, plump Buck Mulligan, no Leopold Bloom, and especially no Molly Bloom. There are elder statesmen to lend a hand, and especially patronage, but it is a thoroughly corrupt system based on influence, including the army that would play such a strong role in Egyptian politics. Marriages bargains between families; a single woman (even one like the sister, whose appearance is consistently disparaged) is a dangerous temptation (which of course makes her prey). Islam is barely a presence, except to the degree that it is reflected in Mahfouz' caustic rendition of the way perceptions of honor plays out in this society. This is a claustrophobic world with economic and social rules so toxic that they pit family against family, boy against girl, brother against brother, (and especially against sister). Joyce wrote of Ireland that she was an old sow that ate its farrow (although that quotation is from "Portrait of an Artist", not "Ulysses"). Mahfouz' Bloom-less and at its rotten foundation honor-less Cairo is something even more dark and distressing: an old sow that encourages its young to take advantage of and then sacrifice each other. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13185311834114378699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2634529928" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2634529928" />
    <a title="Naeem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/217489-naeem"><img alt="Naeem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1186230499p2/217489.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2634529928?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naeem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naeem" href="/user/show/217489-naeem">Naeem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385264587" href="/book/show/7160.The_Beginning_and_the_End">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2634529928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2651381720562552672">Review of Naguib Mahfouz, The Beginning and the End<br/><br/>I read this as a “political economy” novel, but in a very subtle one. Most novels by Third World writers have something to do with either a direct encounter with Westerners or the indirect but total engagement with modernity. While both these elements are present in this novel, they are far in the distance. Instead, Mahfouz foregrounds poverty.<br/><br/>He does so, however, by giving his characters rich inner lives and placing them within a complex social</span>
  <span id="freeText2651381720562552672" style="display:none">Review of Naguib Mahfouz, The Beginning and the End<br /><br />I read this as a “political economy” novel, but in a very subtle one. Most novels by Third World writers have something to do with either a direct encounter with Westerners or the indirect but total engagement with modernity. While both these elements are present in this novel, they are far in the distance. Instead, Mahfouz foregrounds poverty.<br /><br />He does so, however, by giving his characters rich inner lives and placing them within a complex social environment. The usual treatment of poverty is as deprivation, as absence, as an emptiness. Here, instead, the state of poverty is treated as insatiable envy, as stoic courage, as noble sacrifice, as temptation with sexual desire, and as a family’s heroic effort to keep intact what is left of their social status. While the materiality of poverty is elemental to the novel’s fabric, Mahfouz never forgets that poverty is full of philosophy, poetry, ambition, love, grace, and the richness of full life. Maslow’s “hierarchy of needs” dies its natural death here because the simple truth is that all needs are simultaneous. Hunger, sexual desire, and philosophical self-actualization are one. Ignoring this truth is the dirty secret of our condescension towards the poor.<br /><br />Mahfouz’s writing has tremendous narrative drive. He is a master of presenting psychological and social structures as both visible and invisible. Invisible because Mahfouz keeps the reader’s attention focused on the plot and on his exquisite characters; invisible because no act and no thought is presented without its proper social and psychological motivation.<br /><br />The story opens with the death of family breadwinner – a low level bureaucrat whose pension is inadequate to feed and clothe his wife and four children. The question becomes how will the family reorganize themselves so that they can survive on two meals a day while retaining their lower-middle class existence. Three elements are at play in this dynamic: the material weight of survival, the stickiness of trying to retain social standing, and the desperate longing to make it into the middle class. Marx with Veblen and beyond, we might say.<br /><br />Ultimately, Mahfouz shows that the costs of success are so high that its realization is yet another kind of failure. Far, far in the background is the idea that the solution to this problem is some kind of socialism. <br /><br />Fear not though, if you blink you can miss the political economy elements here. But you won’t be any worse for having internalized them without your knowledge. Such is Mahfouz’s artistry.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2651381720562552672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_65301190" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65301190" />
    <a title="Tia Crane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2536179-tia-crane"><img alt="Tia Crane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1248389523p2/2536179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65301190?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tia Crane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tia Crane" href="/user/show/2536179-tia-crane">Tia Crane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

<div id="review_1830162382" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1830162382" />
    <a title="Gordon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6000426-gordon"><img alt="Gordon" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830162382?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gordon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gordon" href="/user/show/6000426-gordon">Gordon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385264587" href="/book/show/7160.The_Beginning_and_the_End">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6000426-gordon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830162382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7508071549220817675">Very heavy going. Partly because of the serious subject matter (this is tragedy writ large, if in a small arena) and partly because of the language. The more Arabic literature I read, the more obvious it becomes that translating must be a real challenge, and few people are up to the task of making it sound natural in English. It's a tribue to Mahfouz's original that, despite his translator's frequently jarring choice of expression, there is still so much life in this book.<br/><br/>Notwithstanding the des</span>
  <span id="freeText7508071549220817675" style="display:none">Very heavy going. Partly because of the serious subject matter (this is tragedy writ large, if in a small arena) and partly because of the language. The more Arabic literature I read, the more obvious it becomes that translating must be a real challenge, and few people are up to the task of making it sound natural in English. It's a tribue to Mahfouz's original that, despite his translator's frequently jarring choice of expression, there is still so much life in this book.<br /><br />Notwithstanding the description offered by Goodreads (taken from the book's foreword), <i>The Beginning and the End</i> has nothing to do with the Second World War, which as such is not even mentioned. The setting is ordinary middle-class Egyptian life in the 1930s. Ordinary, that is, aside from the death that plunges a family into unexpected povery - and the sometimes tragic choices made as they struggle to survive and return to 'respectability'. In various ways, its characters fall victim to expectations, both their own and those of others, expectations about social status, about the role of women, about family. It is striking that the one person who remains clear headed (at no small cost) is the mother, Samira - and that, at the same time, she seems oblivious to her children's inner worlds.<br /><br />Could anyone have chosen differently? What choices, if any, might have led to a happier ending? What choices, if any, might we want to reconsider ourselves? Those are the questions Mahfouz left with me, questions that - despite some culturally-specific details in the plot - are truly universal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7508071549220817675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_429400227" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/429400227" />
    <a title="Геллее Салахов Авбакар" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3767491"><img alt="Геллее Салахов Авбакар" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523374851p2/3767491.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/429400227?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Геллее Салахов Авбакар" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Геллее Салахов Авбакар" href="/user/show/3767491">Геллее Салахов Авбакар</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9773161285" href="/book/show/9433994">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3767491?shelf=arab-literature">arab-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer429400227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11385388999269582938"><b>Disclosure:</b><br/>I came across this nice story of NAGIB MAHFOUZ During my Tour in Morocco, I was much devoted to the Arabic Literature I bought it with 6 Euro. with the same features above. <br/><br/><b>My Plot:</b><br/>First of all, I would say that all the stories narrated by NAGIB MAHFOUZ happens in Poor neighborhood in Egypt; In fact "Bidaya Wa Nihaya" was a direct criticism to this life in General. The story begins with the Death of the Father, Three children and a Daughter were under the responsibility of the Mother.</span>
  <span id="freeText11385388999269582938" style="display:none"><b>Disclosure:</b><br />I came across this nice story of NAGIB MAHFOUZ During my Tour in Morocco, I was much devoted to the Arabic Literature I bought it with 6 Euro. with the same features above. <br /><br /><b>My Plot:</b><br />First of all, I would say that all the stories narrated by NAGIB MAHFOUZ happens in Poor neighborhood in Egypt; In fact "Bidaya Wa Nihaya" was a direct criticism to this life in General. The story begins with the Death of the Father, Three children and a Daughter were under the responsibility of the Mother. Hassan, Housein, Hassanin, and Nafisa were Characters of different dimensions, First the Mother worked hard to make the Family overcome the difficulties of life, Hassan worked as a Musician inside a popular party group, he was so adorable to his father until he becomes one of the bitters inside the family, Housein was a mighty man who feels the need of the family and worked hard to overcome poverty, He was the best Characters inside the story, the Latter was Hassanin, a very cruel and rude one, he didn't like the way the family lives in, he was always against the rules, He came to be a sub-officer inside the Egyptian army but Life goes against him as well he fall in love with a girl inside the Bourgeois class but that love came to be the principles of his end; Nafisa the Only daughter inside the family worked as a tailor, but later she falls in a falsified love with a shop keeper who deceive her, in the last moment she begin having promiscuous relations for the sake of money. and thus the life of the family came to an end after being a united family during the life of it's main keeper (the father). <br /><br /><b>Positive and Negative Aspects:</b><br />Speaking of Positive aspects I would say the Following, the flow of events and the nature of story telling are all amazing, they seem entirely held by a professional writer, besides, the nature of story telling sometimes held by the characters themselves, and that's what represent the Touch of modernity inside MAHFOUZ books. Concerning the negative aspects, I would admit that story was a complete tragedy, the writer take no mercy or any slow feeling to the Characters, It was so harsh from the beginning to the End like the story title. Besides the Story inflect the real nature of the Egyptian society towards orphans in General. Generally reading this story would make you revolt and go against anything that relates to poverty.<br /><br /><b>My Personal Reaction:</b><br />Reading this story would make you feel sad to most extent, I really took mercy upon the Characters, It was like they were paying the sins that they do not commit at all, having a girl who make promiscuous relations for the sake of money, a very harsh society that looks only for the sake of it's profit, a worthless religion that take no effect upon it's followers and so on and so forth, all these circumstances plays indirectly inside the events of the story, But what inspires me the most was the sudden attack that the writer had toward his own society, Attacking through literature was a nice mindful step. Generally the story was a complete tragedy that no nice event would go inside it. So it is worthy to feel it inside. <br /><br /><b>Recommendations:</b> <br />The story is written in Arabic so I don't recommend to all the Audience, However I would recommend it to people who had a prior knowledge of the Arab world in general and the Egyptian society particularly, Though I will stay tuned to any of our readers who might need help to understand it. Otherwise it would be worthy for the Arab themselves to read about their tragic past.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11385388999269582938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_117073521" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117073521" />
    <a title="Tyler " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1096417-tyler"><img alt="Tyler " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377822301p2/1096417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117073521?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tyler " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tyler " href="/user/show/1096417-tyler">Tyler </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385264587" href="/book/show/7160.The_Beginning_and_the_End">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tyler  by: </span>
      Author's Reputation
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1096417-tyler?shelf=superb">superb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1096417-tyler?shelf=literature">literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117073521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4504424279728384177">Four passions drive the plot of this book, a realistic and linear narrative by the Arab world’s greatest novelist. The book tells the story, set in the mid-1930's, of a middle class Cairo family hit by a recent misfortune. The passions are those of the four children approaching young adulthood.<br/> <br/>If the genre is realism, an unmistakable tinge of naturalism also infuses this tale. The Freudian idea of human "drives" fascinated writers at the time, including Naguib Mahfouz. As the story develops, th</span>
  <span id="freeText4504424279728384177" style="display:none">Four passions drive the plot of this book, a realistic and linear narrative by the Arab world’s greatest novelist. The book tells the story, set in the mid-1930's, of a middle class Cairo family hit by a recent misfortune. The passions are those of the four children approaching young adulthood.<br /> <br />If the genre is realism, an unmistakable tinge of naturalism also infuses this tale. The Freudian idea of human "drives" fascinated writers at the time, including Naguib Mahfouz. As the story develops, the drives that animate each of the children come into focus: One has an instinct for crime, another a need for conformity, a third a blinding ambition, and the fourth an intense sex drive. The family meets some success as it pulls together to get through tough times, more perhaps than the mother has expected. But another thing the mother hasn’t anticipated is an emerging clash of desires.<br /> <br />Can each son or daughter achieve independence in life or, as one son wonders, <i>do we humans devour each other</i>? What does it mean to help your family? What kinds of rights do we have to our own happiness? The plot seems to push toward some happy medium. But in the end, there’s one loose thread that starts to unravel, and it’s not the one readers are led to expect.<br /> <br />The book starts simply as the author sets the stage. Then the plot moves faster as the story progresses, and the climax at the end is shocking enough to feel like a body blow. This is one of three books I’ve read, <i>A Tale of Two Cities</i> and <i>Sons and Lovers</i> being the other two, where the last pages are so well done they deserve special note. The effect of the denouement lingers and takes time to digest.<br /> <br />Readers get a sense here of the unusual compassion Mahfouz harbors for all the book's characters and for the human condition. He says nothing overtly; he just relates the details of the lives concerned, and those details connect with our own. No action is so depraved that the writing doesn’t bring you face-to-face with its essential human origin. A motif of propriety, a sense of what's shameful or indecent, lurks in the background: Is it a disgrace, for instance, to <i>have</i> to work, or to be unable to marry? This motif asserts itself more and more as the story nears its appointed end.<br /> <br />As usual for Mahfouz, this book gives Westerners easy access to a world different from ours, yet with universal qualities. Again I harp on this point, because non-Western literature really does seem like something we wouldn’t easily relate to. And again, this is a good book with which to branch out from one's many comfort zones. Arabic readers need no encouragement, so for my part I'd like to recommend this book to all the others out there who have yet to pick up a Mahfouz novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4504424279728384177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_104641628" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104641628" />
    <a title="surfmadpig" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3795194-surfmadpig"><img alt="surfmadpig" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275072916p2/3795194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104641628?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="surfmadpig" class="user" itemprop="url" name="surfmadpig" href="/user/show/3795194-surfmadpig">surfmadpig</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789607021717" href="/book/show/8357618">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3795194-surfmadpig?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3795194-surfmadpig?shelf=read-in-greek">read-in-greek</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3795194-surfmadpig?shelf=read-in-translation">read-in-translation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104641628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3306718375648899186">I have mixed feelings about this book. I'd read a short story by Mahfouz in English and really liked it, so I thought I should try one of his novels. <br/><br/>Unfortunately, the Greek translation is awful; not only is it clear the translator is not that familiar with the Greek language, but the person who got paid for doing the corrections and the editing clearly didn't do a thing. And yes, we're talking about very annoying errors, the kind that any reader would notice, not just a translator. <br/><br/>But I'll tr</span>
  <span id="freeText3306718375648899186" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about this book. I'd read a short story by Mahfouz in English and really liked it, so I thought I should try one of his novels. <br /><br />Unfortunately, the Greek translation is awful; not only is it clear the translator is not that familiar with the Greek language, but the person who got paid for doing the corrections and the editing clearly didn't do a thing. And yes, we're talking about very annoying errors, the kind that any reader would notice, not just a translator. <br /><br />But I'll try to speak about the book itself. The writing felt simple, perhaps simplistic at times, as did the plot. However, there was something that kept me reading; it was probably the characters: very real and very convincing, the kind that invokes strong feelings in the reader. Upon completing the novel, I realized that it is not as simplistic as it seemed. <br /><br />It wasn't hard to remember that this was written in Egypt in 1950, and not only due to the setting. In Mahfouz's novel there are some things a contemporary writer would avoid like the plague, telling the reader straight out what a character thinks, for instance. Still, for some reason, it works. It wasn't as brilliant as I had expected, but it still worked despite it all.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3306718375648899186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_730117963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/730117963" />
    <a title="Lois" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11970342-lois"><img alt="Lois" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345242614p2/11970342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/730117963?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lois" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lois" href="/user/show/11970342-lois">Lois</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385264587" href="/book/show/7160.The_Beginning_and_the_End">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer730117963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12179492993075008606">To paraphrase someone, a great writer makes the universal specific and the specific universal. This novel succeeds magnificently. The story begins with a standard family disaster in Cairo in the mid-1930s. The father, a minor government official, suddenly dies. His family slips into penurious poverty in short order. Much of what happens to them would be familiar to any suddenly income-less household in the USA or elsewhere. Any character defects are magnified by their suffering, with little hope</span>
  <span id="freeText12179492993075008606" style="display:none">To paraphrase someone, a great writer makes the universal specific and the specific universal. This novel succeeds magnificently. The story begins with a standard family disaster in Cairo in the mid-1930s. The father, a minor government official, suddenly dies. His family slips into penurious poverty in short order. Much of what happens to them would be familiar to any suddenly income-less household in the USA or elsewhere. Any character defects are magnified by their suffering, with little hope and no remediation. The Nobel-Prize-winning Mahfouz demonstrates a strong sensitivity to the plight of women, either within the family or struggling to earn a living, and does not shy away from describing what happens to vulnerable women, even those who seem to be well-placed and provided for. Mahfouz does not proselytize, but makes clear that what happens to these women is due in part to them being denied an education or agency. <br />This novel also provides some historical background about Egypt. The societal place of military officers, riots and demonstrations, corruption--these are all themes in this book, just as they are in Egypt right now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12179492993075008606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_783542404" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/783542404" />
    <a title="J.M. Hushour" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17463213-j-m-hushour"><img alt="J.M. Hushour" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442964894p2/17463213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/783542404?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.M. Hushour" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.M. Hushour" href="/user/show/17463213-j-m-hushour">J.M. Hushour</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385264587" href="/book/show/7160.The_Beginning_and_the_End">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer783542404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer884463787814190111">This is a tremendous, tremendous novel. If you're into exploring the abysses of human nature, look no further than here, though the pay-off is near the end, abrupt, climactic and horrifying. The story is simple, pure Mahfouz: a patriarch dies suddenly, leaving his wife, three sons and his daughter destitute and struggling in 1930s Cairo. The three sons, almost Dostoevskyian archetypes are the Criminal/Louse, the Practical One, and the Passionate One. The daughter, physically wanting, yet devoted</span>
  <span id="freeText884463787814190111" style="display:none">This is a tremendous, tremendous novel. If you're into exploring the abysses of human nature, look no further than here, though the pay-off is near the end, abrupt, climactic and horrifying. The story is simple, pure Mahfouz: a patriarch dies suddenly, leaving his wife, three sons and his daughter destitute and struggling in 1930s Cairo. The three sons, almost Dostoevskyian archetypes are the Criminal/Louse, the Practical One, and the Passionate One. The daughter, physically wanting, yet devoted to the family is tragedy anthropomorphized. The story is of their struggle to make ends meet in various ways while trying to hold on to some inkling of the dreams of their previous life. It is the latter that drives the book's insanity. For all the good you think you are doing, no matter how you're doing it, it can lead to nothing but darkness. Probably Mahfouz's crowning achievement, overflowing with a humanity that Children of Gebelawi lacks, for instance.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="884463787814190111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_4637889" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4637889" />
    <a title="Shawne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/284285-shawne"><img alt="Shawne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1187283272p2/284285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4637889?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawne" href="/user/show/284285-shawne">Shawne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385264587" href="/book/show/7160.The_Beginning_and_the_End">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Naguib Mahfouz fans, people visiting Egypt</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/284285-shawne?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4637889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3130542847380973303">I picked this up in a Cairo bookstore to complete the whole Egyptian experience. Relentlessly depressing - a look at one family's descent into poverty following the death of the father. Okay enough, but I must have been missing something in the translation - the language felt very textbook and colourless to me.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_237228741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237228741" />
    <a title="Ghadeer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5612842-ghadeer"><img alt="Ghadeer" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237228741?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ghadeer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ghadeer" href="/user/show/5612842-ghadeer">Ghadeer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5612842-ghadeer?shelf=arabic">arabic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237228741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer858738826991668494">This is the first classical arabic novel I read, with a taste very different to English novels that took a while to get used to but left me captivated. I love the way the author showed how each character's priorities and behaviour changed differently in response to the situations they're put in, and the gloomy ending was suitable to the direction the story was going despite being such a shocker. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_410471460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/410471460" />
    <a title="Nelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9782004-nelly"><img alt="Nelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529030355p2/9782004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/410471460?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nelly" href="/user/show/9782004-nelly">Nelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer410471460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18338755275429650614">Reading English version. A slow book, maybe not the best translation, but has a lingering effect on me. The way Mafouz can disassemble and reassemble the emotions of his characters is masterful. Through his characters, he can pound the same issues (abject poverty, frustration, despair, small joys) from so many different angles so that light is shed each time. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

So, I read the book.<br/><br/>Original Arabic Bidaya wa-Nihaya published 1949. This translation from 1985. Won a Nobel Prize for Literature. I did not read paperback. My local library connection found a hard cover.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, the issues presented in this book are still relevant 2019. Sad.</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4L+oJqMZcah1C48gz1rJSZT7X3kMWBv8xN6vjuSQXrWyGd5jsZJz6ZkbLAacqzXnaz4AOtNKWN7InEs64Xu0Qg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mSATo5brKuEon3byjUVtCeInNJcPL3/L4AZ6ZVM48vzLhmXmhGAooMSP1dTetJGnHeJr1NA9POnsRJ7RVtMYCw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4398419052301755435">Naguib Mahfouz (Arabic author profile: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273240._' rel='nofollow noopener'>نجيب محفوظ</a>) was an Egyptian writer who won the 1988 Nobel Prize for Literature. He published over 50 novels, over 350 short stories, dozens of movie scripts, and five plays over a 70-year career. Many of his works have been made into Egyptian and foreign films.</span>
  <span id="freeText4398419052301755435" style="display:none">Naguib Mahfouz (Arabic author profile: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273240._" rel="nofollow noopener">نجيب محفوظ</a>) was an Egyptian writer who won the 1988 Nobel Prize for Literature. He published over 50 novels, over 350 short stories, dozens of movie scripts, and five plays over a 70-year career. Many of his works have been made into Egyptian and foreign films.</span>
